## \#18 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-04-22T23:42:06.373Z Reads: 505

```
[quote="trbt555, post:13, topic:2510, full:true"]
Just use a gps cycle computer and you have what you need.
[/quote]

Exactly, you can download free apps that have a speed reading that is very accurate.

Also, with the emergence of apple watch & android watch it would be rather easy to develop an app that has all the speed related data on your wrist.

ALSO With gyros & accelerometers in your phone you could probably also get this data:
- G force
- Hoprsepower
- deduce a torque measurement
- Possibly even a fuel gauge based on timeXmovementXaverage power consumption.

The app might get you to perform some simple calibrations, such as a 100m sprint, enter body weight, wheel size, 


Someone better at maths & physics could probably elaborate on this further....

[LIST OF COMMON SENSORS IN ANDROID](http://developer.android.com/guide/topics/sensors/sensors_overview.html)
```

## \#57 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-04-30T10:11:51.639Z Reads: 357

```
[quote="loose_nickers, post:56, topic:2510"]
Aren't they designed in Australia?
[/quote]

Yeah but that is not really the whole story is it?

example: my boards are designed in Australia too, they are assembled here too, but i source majority of parts from china, the motor controller is custom made (now in USA) designed in Sweden, the battery cells are Korean & assembled in china. 

To give you some insights to the origins of the evolve technology have a look at this post, the didn't really design anything to begin with... Even now their motors are commonly seen on most "china" style eboards.

http://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/are-diy-electric-skateboards-cheaper-the-false-economy/165/23?u=onloop
```

## \#61 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-04-30T14:36:15.525Z Reads: 354

```
[quote="OwenGrady, post:58, topic:2510"]
And Evolve has to thank Enertion?
[/quote]

Hi Owen, Do you work for evolve? 

anyway... the truth is I really love what evolve are doing, I look up to what Jeff has done & it inspires me to grow & build a legit brand & business just like he has.... I have got a lot of catching up to do though! Evolve is proably 100X bigger than enertion in terms of sales & revenue. I'm just a small guy!

I do know how hard Jeff has had to work to get his business where it is today... I love that he is about to release a new model.... I haven't been this excited in a while, it will fuel my passion even further to make the best electric skateboards I can from my little garage..... & I do love a good challenge.

So YES, in many ways I am trying to emulate what Jeff is doing, but I am also walking my own path... I am probably more focussed on the community & educating people about how to build their own esk8... Jeff has not taken that direction.

& I think If you asked Jeff honestly what he thinks about enertion (me) so far, I think he would admit that I am doing a good job... Take his new product release as an example, a dual drive esk8 with brushless outrunners.... If he thought what I was doing is shit why would he do it too? I am sure his new deck will be awesome & it will likely slow down the Raptor sales... & I dare say Raptor sales has probably slowed down Evolve sales a tad. I will need to get smarter & I will need to hone my business acumen.... it's very exciting.

Deep down we are all here because we love esk8! Hopefully, one day soon Jeff & I can have a beer and talk shop.... I am sure we would get on very well.

Until then we will both be working tirelessly to make the best esk8 we can.... Competition is great for innovation... & its great for the consumer.

So lets do it! Enertion VS Evolve! Aussie VS Aussie... Watch out world...We will show you what passion & drive can deliver! If anyone should be worried it should be BB

I am ready... is evolve :)
```

```
my design is a physical expression of my own desires, this object was not created to please everyone, pleasing everyone is impossible.
```

## \#64 Posted by: OwenGrady Posted at: 2016-04-30T18:03:30.144Z Reads: 333

```
Hi BrabRS, onloop & monkey32. Also anyone else who cares to know.

Do I work for evolve? No. But I'll concede I like to think I'm not far from the group. For now though, just a very satisfied customer.

Am I team Evolve? Damn straight. Seemingly as much so as monkey32 is for team Enertion.

I have been lurking the forums for a long while yes, and at one stage considered going the DIY route.. But I rode a bamboo street, and for me the deal was done.  What they did with 350w makes me doubt the need for some of the silly numbers I hear thrown about. I am happy to pay a brand who know their stuff for a board I just want to ride, and I'm super excited for what comes next, even if it does have silly numbers attached.
I more peruse this forum for interest and lately the fact that a search for evolve's new board info brought me to this topic. As with every forum, I am entitled to comment my opinions, and wield my keyboard sword if the time requires.  I found this topic to be that time.

@brabrs I have no specs to provide, sorry to spoil your hopes! Though I did fluke a chance to see some testing of the board a few months back, I can definitely say they haven't taken baby steps with this one. Call the guys at the shop, you'll hear even they are intimidated by what it can do, and they are all passionate electric skaters! I'm sure Jeff will show this when the time is right, but I guess that's fine for you cause evolve clearly doesn't excite you anyway.

@onloop Firstly, credit to your response. With previous statements, I will admit the vibe I was expecting was quite different to what you did actually say. You have done a huge job with the forum, and the positivity in your response I hope was genuine.  I understand this is your forum, but you know evolve has a huge customer/fan base that are very passionate about the brand.  Making public a mockery of their video where they take no shots at you, is interesting business tact. While I don't know you, or really have a negative opinion of you personally, you are picking a fight with this video, and the evolve mob won't like it. I'm merely pointing out that making a claim as such, and a video parody, hoping it results in a friendly chat and a beer.. might not really add up to the positive relationship you intend. I've only met Jeff a handful of times and he is very protective of his work. If evolve is 100x bigger, I'd be careful claiming the chicken or the egg, because clearly he is doing something right.  I do wish you luck with your raptor, hopefully it will be competitive to the market, but right now evolve is definitely the bigger fish.


Oh and monkey32, about that science lesson.. Dinosaurs may have evolved into 'birds of prey', but apes evolved into today's apex predators.. See how those dinosaur teeth go against the human's technological ability to kill anything. We are the modern apex predator & top of the food chain.  Though by name, it seems you only got as far as the peeling bananas stage.. Maybe next time, for now best keep big bird on Sesame Street ðŸ˜‰ 
I'd shut up, but class is still in session.
```

```
[quote="OwenGrady, post:64, topic:2510"]
Making public a mockery of their video where they take no shots at you, is interesting business tact. While I don't know you, or really have a negative opinion of you personally, you are picking a fight with this video, and the evolve mob won't like it.
[/quote]

Welcome to the community Owen. 

My response above is genuine. It would be an honour to meet Jeff... I would certainly buy him a beer. I am not a hater.

My parody video is a simple marketing tactic.. the more people I can get talking about eboard performance the more people I will be able to educate & offer my service to... brand loyalty only goes so far.

Jeff knows performance matters, If he didn't think it mattered he would not be releasing the new & improved model primarily promising improvements in performance as the key feature. This is happening because his loyal customer base are now demanding better, the customer knowledge is evolving faster than the company.. 

Honestly, Who doesn't want more speed & performance? I bet you do? This community is proof of that. The viewership here is skyrocketing! 40k last month... 1700 people just yesterday reading about how to make high-performance electric skateboards.

At this point I think jeff doesn't have an option, he must deliver better performance.... or loose market share.

So if we are scoring the battle so far, it seems I've won round one already.... the audience wants more power & performance and I have written that script. You are an example of that... you are here now & the conversation about performance has already started... that is my primary objective. Educating the masses about what's possible in the world of esk8.

I put my eggs in the performance basket. Jeff has followed. The question is whether evolve is nimble enough! Will they be able to keep up? 

I imagine evolve has some massive overheads, they must also keep the COGS low as their business model relies heavily on wholesale channels. Unfortunately, high performance also equals high cost. So they are going to have some big pricing decisions to make.... they need to maintain healthy margins because they have a big bunch of resellers to keep happy. If their cost base increases just $100 that could push their retail price up an extra $400. The only way they can achieve high performance and keep their offering at current pricing is by investing in a huge amount of stock & mass producing parts (or using low-tech stuff).. this locks them into their "version" of technology for extended periods. Its a problem all tech companies have when they are bigger, how to scale & stay relevant?. It's hard to continually evolve when you have certain business constraints that prevent rapid evolution...

Enertion is small enough & nimble enough to turn on a dime. Our battery tech, motor controllers, power management technology & battery chemistry tech will constantly evolve.... 

The irony is enertion may evolve faster than evolve can. I don't really see how enertion can loose...
```

## \#73 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-05-01T00:33:28.073Z Reads: 309

```
[quote="OwenGrady, post:71, topic:2510"]
Evolve set the bar for performance
[/quote]

no, they didn't.... I suppose it depends on what your definition of performance is.

they do deserve credit for their carbon deck design with integrated battery! that was a really nice move.... they were the first in the world to do it... 

They also decided to improve the battery chemistry & capacity extending the ride time! that was smart!

they invested in molds to remake their hand controller! smart move! that helped to differentiate them from a growing market of me-too copycats.

But they kept the same motor controller & brick-like motor that all the other "players" like fiik, altered, exkate were using... that is what has held them back!

yeah, they upgraded their trucks with gullwing sidewinder clones & put on some nice urethane! they deserve credit for all that....

But, when it comes to the performance, it was pretty much the same as the rest of the mass produced china products... same motors, same motor controllers & same hand controller. (hence the new version - jeff is smart, he knows what his weakness is)

If I really wanted I could also start selling the same "evolve" drive train system tomorrow.. here is the Chinese factory that makes it

https://kaxamoto.en.alibaba.com/product/1812912213-212664882/Electric_Skateboards_for_Sale_280W_500W.html

BUT at enertion we choose not to get the cookie cutter option available to every man, I choose to make my own creation! Because at heart I am a true electric skateboard builder.... from the ground up.

The difference is I tell my various factories what I want them to make, I don't simply buy the mass produced product that they are offering to anyone who thinks they can make a quick buck. Everything (90%) is custom made to my spec. 

This is why it is so hard for others to copy enertion... My advantage is constant innovation and a stubborn "I can make it better" attitude.
```

## \#85 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-01T06:33:52.865Z Reads: 288

```
Interesting topic, indeed. IMO, defending a mass produced, corporate product as better than enertions stuff is laughable. The reality is, like @onloop said, evolve can't turn on a dime, and switch things up too much. You have to be willing to go out on a limb. Still to this day, I have yet to see anyone else integrate working head/brake lights inside of an electric skateboard except me (I'm talking about lights inside of the pressed portion of the deck, not below or on the trucks). No one needs lights, but they are cheap to add, and make night time riding much safer and easier. I know, some big company will do this before I even have a chance to start an llc, and put this into into the market. I when I try to say that I had this idea first, some fan boy will come along and complain that "x, y, or z did it first". The reality is, the DYI community has technology far greater than the corporate community. By the time companies like inboard get their "new hub technology" shipped, the DYI community will have (and does have) a handful of hub motors much better.

@OwenGrady it's a bummer that you have the outlook you have on eskates. You think you know best, but your ignoring the fact that corporations have bottom lines, which is money. DYI companies also have bottom lines, improving technology and offering the best possible tech to their customers. and that is what @onloop has done.
```

## \#119 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-05-09T02:23:15.824Z Reads: 282

```

Looks like the 7-inch pneumatic is actually using 5mm pitch pulley.... ballsy move...

this video below i posted back in 2014 has 5mm pitch pulleys & 5.5inch pneumatic wheels... i eventually stopped using this system due to rocks getting caught in the belt. Evolve do have a cover over the motor pulley but there is still a big gap between the wheel pulley & motor pulley...

Overall though i think the drive train looks good, having the machined step for the pulley bearing is smart.
```

## \#152 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-12T16:22:02.879Z Reads: 262

```
What keeps me away from making budget DIY builds is I actually need to use these things for daily commuting, not recreation (although I would). To try to use your first DIY build as a legitimate commuting vehicle is a big risk. It runs the possibility of breaking down easier or at the worst possible time compared to completes made by companies which have tested all their parts for years.

I think the DIY community will always consist of mostly engineer type folks that were already into building stuff not related to esk8. Those type of folks are the ones that can make quality builds that don't break down or look like s#!7. I want something that doesn't look like s#!7 and completes are my best bet at the moment.
```

## \#168 Posted by: longhairedboy Posted at: 2016-05-12T19:11:18.377Z Reads: 253

```
[quote="torqueboards, post:165, topic:2510"]
I really think everyone should move away from Lithium Ion and just go A123 cells. Those 1,000 cycle life cells are amazing compared to a Lithium Ion pack (although bigger) in size.
[/quote]

which A123 cells? Thier 18650s are lifepo4 apparently, their 26650s are lithium ion, or so the site says, but its some nanophosphate thing and they say it has 10X the cycle life. But they also only have a nominal voltage of 3.3v and a lower mah rating and discharge rating than the sammy INRs .. and they're waaaay more expensive. ITs kind of a tough call to go with them, and i'm having a tough time making the case for them in my head at the moment. 

i just bought 50 sammy INR18650-25R cells for $242 tax and shipping included. I'm trying to find out how much 50 of those A123 18650s would be. A guy brought a solar powered rig by my shop not too long ago with 12 of those 26650s and i wish i could recall exactly what he paid, but it was somewhere close to that.

They need to come down in price and come up in discharge performance. Then they will have me.
```

## \#169 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-12T19:25:35.040Z Reads: 256

```
What I meant by the commuting comment was really that something I (a potential DIY builder) would make is more likely to break down than something a reputable company (Evolve) would make. Add in the fact that I'd have a warranty and could just ship the board to get fixed no problem/no time spent testing things and it becomes practical for the average person who has a 9-5 and other priorities than messing with what's supposed to (or should) be a reliable commuting vehicle.

As far as the power, they did mention that it climbs 25% grade hills..
> Firstly, the dual brushless motors power the board up insanely steep hills of up to 25 degree gradient with ease.

Which would basically make this board a slightly faster/better looking/heavier  d+ with nearly 9 times the range. Perfect. 

Yes, DIY builds have more power and can be customized, but not every person that wants to get into esk8 can make something better than the carbon for a first or even second build. If they could, they should probably be selling completes themselves lol
```

## \#223 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-13T17:34:10.822Z Reads: 231

```
After rereading *again* I saw this bit:

> The street wheels can be swapped over for off-road tires when the rider is headed for rougher terrain, but this time around Evolve has made that process a little easier. It mightn't sound like much, but both types of wheel work with the same trucks, or hangers, meaning you won't need to swap those over in addition to the wheels and belt. **All up, a tire-change pitstop took us under 10 minutes. With the street wheels attached, the GT not only goes faster, handles better and just feels smoother to ride, it will also go much further with each charge.**

This seems to suggest that the street wheels indeed will give you the higher end of the advertised speed, despite their conflicting statement near the end. We will see, but it only make sense considering the board has to work harder to power the AT wheels and is practically pushing it to its limits -- hence why the range is reduced with them on.
```

## \#252 Posted by: Mickyboy Posted at: 2016-05-14T00:38:34.541Z Reads: 210

```
The board I tested had the beta motors I believe, the production motors will be a little different. I didn't test the beta board back to back with the Raptor but I can say that it has plenty of power and torque, at least as much as my Boosted Dual Plus, and enough to keep me happy. According to specs the Raptor is more powerful again, but all the other advantages of the Evolve GT make it an easy decision for me as to which one I'd prefer. Remember this is just my opinion.
```

```
Thanks!

Matt
Evolve Skateboards Australia
```

## \#298 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-14T17:12:49.288Z Reads: 215

```
Saw this under the shipping tab on their website for the previous carbon series. This seems to be their international shipping policy, not sure if this will be how we get the boards if they plan on keeping the boards in Australia:

> INTERNATIONAL SHIPPING: 

> International deliveries of electric skateboards are sent via Fedex and take approx. 2-6 days depending on your location.  Accessories are also sent via Fedex and take approx. 2 -6 days shipping.

> PLEASE NOTE: Some countries may have addition duties, taxes or other charges applied through customs. We do not cover those costs and advise that you contact your country's customs office if you are unsure of what they may be.

> If your country isn't listed please contact us for pricing.

> Prices are in $AUD and shipping is applied to your order at the END of the checkout process once you've entered your address.

> Please note the prices below include a $105 Dangerous Goods Fedex fee due to sending lithium batteries internationally.

> Shipping rates for Electric Skateboards via Fedex
> Zone C	Japan	$285
> Zone D	US, Canada	$380
> Zone E	France, UK, Germany	$380
> Zone F	Brazil	$450
> Zone G	UAE	$495
```

## \#328 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-15T02:04:24.453Z Reads: 190

```
No problem. As far as I see it here are the Pros and Cons of both Evolve and Enertion's top offerings (based off what I've seen/heard):

**Raptor Dual**

Pros
- King of torque, flys up hill like they don't exist
- Highest top speed out of every commercially available board
- Swappable, long lasting battery
- Customizable to no end 
- Relatively light, 1 more pound than a d+
- Kicktail....enough said. 

Cons
- Some report it does not feel like a longboard, but more like a platform (hoverboard? lol)
- Fast charger has a noisy fan
- Not great for low speed cruising 
- Not beginner friendly

**Evolve GT**

Pros
- Longest range of any board available (except metroboard, but it is nearly 23 f*** pounds!!) 
- High top speed
- Can take 25%+ grade hills like a bo$$
- Sexy as fuck
- Ability to switch between AT and street wheels
- Remote LCD with trip distance/speed/battery percentage and voltage
- Gullwing trucks, carving heaven

Cons
- Still a bit heavy, 17lbs
- Fast charger takes 3 hours...although you will likely not need to do more than 1 charge lol

Of course, we don't know everything about the GT yet, but basically it comes down to this: **are you a speed demon or a commuter?**
```

## \#355 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-16T04:03:52.216Z Reads: 182

```
This was already posted, the video is not quite fair and likely misrepresented the dual+'s ability to climb hills. However, the Evolve did exceptionally well and it looks like it can easily handle steeper hills which is great. 

I would not go as far as to rate these boards as 1st 2nd 3rd but rather look into what problem they are trying to solve. Enertion is solving the problem for some that want more power in a board -- but don't want to go full DIY because they want a quality, tested, and uniquely designed board with a warranty. Boosted is solving the last mile issue for commuters in Cali that need something relatively light and comfy to ride and get up really steep hills -- but don't need to go far. 

Evolve however lies in the middle. It is not the fastest board out. It does not climb hills as good or better than a raptor. It is not the lightest board either. But it combines what Evolve is know best for (range) and all of the competitions strengths in lesser forms to make the ultimate commuter board for everyone. That being said, I like to go fast and for long distances, so I will be getting both :)
```

However it is far out of my price range and I already have my own custom board which I can easily add more batteries too for more range. So I will stick with my own board until something better comes out. With that stated I favor Enertion out of all electric skateboard companies, so it will probs been one of their boards.

```
At the end of the day you are all right and it comes down to what people want out if the board. 
For me it's an overall experience. I want the power there when I want it, I want it to be fun, I like the idea of carving off road and I like the idea of being as close to snowboarding as possible without actually doing it. 
Like many on here, I look at DIY options, but also liking the idea of buying something ready to go that could fit the bill. 

The release date can't come soon enough. I'm in Australia so hoping can get access to try one asap.
```

## \#362 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-16T12:14:42.487Z Reads: 181

```
Maybe I haven't ridden enough skateboards yet, but carving ability for me had more to do with my truck/bushing set up rather than the material of my deck. The Boosted has a bamboo deck as well, but it has little to do with how easily I can carve. I guess feel is subjective, but I barely stood in the middle of my deck where I could actually feel the flex so it wasn't very useful unless I was going slow in a straight line. That being said, the caliber II's on the BB are HORRIBLE for carving lol I had to switch to Carver CX trucks which have a really narrow wheelbase but are just like the sidewinders on the Evolve -- except more stable even while being loose. The rebound (how quickly you return to center) was insane.

I guarantee you could still get that surfy feel no matter what eboard you have as long as you can switch the truck and upgrade the bushings, it makes such a huge difference. What Evolve has done is put one of the most surfy trucks out there on an esk8, making the ride right out of the box feel smooth as hell. You can do this on any board though.

People can test all they want, really wish it was just the Evolve going up a hill, because that is all that mattered. The Evolve went up that hill like no ones business, and that was exciting to watch.

I'm sure the Raptor can be ridden like a bamboo if you want it to, its just because of the torque and speed keeping the trucks loose would be a nightmare when going fast. I can handle loose trucks at 20mph, but at 25-28 I think I'd fear for my life. That being said, I honestly think the carbon would work fine for you. But they are coming out with a bamboo version as well, so maybe that would suit you better.
```

## \#364 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-16T12:43:55.361Z Reads: 183

```
Of course, one of my main reasons (besides getting an eboard asap) was to do reviews/tests on it against the raptor. Originally, it was just gonna be the raptor vs the d+ (which would've been useless), then it was gonna be the new version (but then the evolve announced), and now it is this lol.

As far as I'm concerned, the Evolve is a slightly punchier board than the d+ (on paper) so comparing it to a Raptor should pretty much sum up the difference between all boards in that spec range in terms of power -- which should be useful. I got over the d+'s low maneuverability by switching the front truck. I can't exactly make 90 degree turns, but I never have to slow down to make an adjustment. Not exactly sure what using the kicktail for those turns would look like in traffic. 

This is not easy for me financially but right now I am losing out on opportunities to do things I've really wanted to do which are: grow my youtube channel more (at 225 subs now, would get more exposure since the board is new), tour DC more for photography (bike riding is not fun), and try commuting from home to work without any public transportation (would save a lot of money daily). Those are all big goals and worth the financial risk in my opinion as they could all pay off for me in the long run. That being said, I might sell one after I've compared them both and seen how they fit into my lifestyle. Hell, I might even try out whatever Boosted has if it turns out to be worth a try. 

AT wheels will take my riding to another level entirely. In DC sidewalks during the summer are PACKED. Around the national mall there is a lot of open grass, and a lot of stony sidewalks that are really shitty to ride on with street wheels. I would be able to plow through all the grass areas and go over rough pavement with ease -- definitely looking forward to it. 

@Ermac-514 If it turns out the 2k version includes everything, I will have both and do testing. I believe getting accurate top speed, torque, etc for all wheel set ups will be very useful for everyone so I'd like to get it all if possible.
```

## \#419 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-17T17:10:23.423Z Reads: 173

```
Technically, if your read the California e-board law that was passed recently, they define what is an electric skateboard near the beginning as... 

"An â€œelectrically motorized boardâ€ is any wheeled device that has a 
floorboard designed to be stood upon when riding that is not greater 
than 60 inches deep and 18 inches wide, is designed to transport only 
one person, and has an electric propulsion system averaging less than 1,000 
watts, the maximum speed of which, when powered solely by a propulsion 
system on a paved level surface, is no more than 20 miles per hour"

Basically, saying that if your board is capable of going more than 20 mph, it does not meet the definition of an "electric skateboard", but rather the old definition of a "motorized skateboard" (you can read on in the law, but it says what doesn't meet this definition is still a motorized skateboard), which this law also affirms is still illegal in California. So technically, the vast majority of e-boards, including practically every diy board, is not legal in California.

Now, It would be hard for a cop to prove your top speed, unless you buy a mass produced board which has their specs advertised online, like evolve.

I get the desire to ride, I get the inability to wait for the next and best, and my hats are off to evolve for finally stepping up to the plate and playing with the big boys. But I doubt their max range is even close to what they are saying. I think they are hyping it up, like every other e-board mass producer out there, to seem way better then it will be. I can go double that speed, with better range, for at least $500 less. Or match the torque with a higher top speed and better range for half the price.

Idk what you are looking for when buying (in my case, building) an e-board, but the 3 numbers that matter to me are torque, top speed, and range. It's hard to compare torque without spending a bunch of money, top speed is usually pretty accurate, but range is like the mpg rating of a car. I could run a board that I wouldn't trust to get me more than 5 miles on my normal route down hills, and get a range of 20 miles. The reality is, when you have 3 mile stretches of up hill, you aren't going to get close to the advertised range rating. So I would like to see the power ratings  (and capacity) of the battery, and the efficiency ratings of their electric system. Until I see that, I don't trust the range they are advertising, and my belief that they are fudging the range numbers makes me distrust any other claims they make about it.
```

---

## \#424 Posted by: Nate Posted at: 2016-05-17T20:44:25.194Z Reads: 175

```
@mr_mahal @michaelinvegas the west side highway ban is actually a little bit more complicated than that. Electric skateboard on the street is already illegal but nypd has a loose policy regarding it, don't cause trouble and they'll leave you alone. It's not the entire bike route of west side highway that ban it, it's the battery city park section that's the most enforced by parks police (in green uniforms). To understand why, you need to know that battery park city(bpc) is not a part of NYC. The property tax we paid living in bpc actually go straight back into battery park city funds rather than the NYC general funds. So the section of the lane along battery park city is jointly maintained AND enforced by bpc and NYC. 

Last year, bpc was ok with riders of electric skateboard on that route because hover board was all the hype and it only goes 7(?)mph. But a few weeks ago, joggers and cyclists living in bpc decided to complain about electric skateboard being a danger to pedestrian because some fuk*ng idiot decided to ride it on the designated pedestrian lane, which prompted bpc to crack down on electric skateboard. Which is bullshit because they're giving a more stringent enforcement due to a few kids fu*king up. 

My feelings regarding Casey Neistat is mix. Love his vlogs but he's a hypocrite. Last year when he got his first board he championed wearing a helmet. A few days later? He stopped wearing it cause it lowers the cool factor. On top of this I see kids imitating his vlogging style by recording themselves carrying their camera on one hand and holding the control with the other. I was shocked. You're going 20+ mph (NYC speed limit is 25 mph btw) and it takes 1 mistake to cause a life and death situation and you're there multi tasking on an eboard. When people idolize you, you have a responsibility to make sure they learn safety too. Especially kids watching his YouTube channel. 

 His new apartment is actually a few blocks from where I live in bpc, so I'm sure he's pretty pissed about the whole situation too. Ironic that he was one of the factors feeding into the problem. Seriously, people do some really dumb shit when they want to show off for camera.
```

## \#430 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-17T21:49:39.959Z Reads: 179

```
[quote="Mr_Mahal, post:423, topic:2510"]
If I want more torque/speed I will use my Raptor -- which if you can beat with your build I fear for your life and safety lol.

I can't say anything I have right now will "beat" the raptor. I can pretty much match it with hummies motors in most aspects (raptor will still beat me on torque) but I can crush the top speed of the raptor with my carvons. I haven't been faster than 35 mph (raptor max is about 27 mph), but in theory, I should be able to reach 66 mph on a full charge.

[quote="Mr_Mahal, post:423, topic:2510"]
Generally speaking giving a solid number for range is pretty much by nature never going to be accurate because of the myriad of factors that go into determining range
[/quote]

My point exactly. Because of that, you can't trust any range number as accurate. Instead, comparing watt hours and the efficiency of the electrical system will tell you more about range then what any company advertises. But since they won't release any specs, there's no way of telling. Based on the size and thickness of the board, I would be surprised if I could get 10 miles from that board on my normal route. With a board that thin, you can only fit so many cells inside. The boards that have good range have huge brick batteries, which is why they are so long.

[quote="Mr_Mahal, post:423, topic:2510"]
You do realize they have to make a profit and provide a warranty right?
[/quote]

I get that, but my point was I could build a board from parts which have warranties (like chakas vescs and carvons hub motors) for far less still.

I will do plenty of tests just for you buddy. We will get to the bottom of this fudgy range.
[/quote]

ok... I'll be waiting... *yawn* I think its going to be while.. By then, this board won't have what everyone else already has.

My whole point is, you've been a fan boy from the beginning, eating up every little detail, and getting so hyped, and trying to hype up everyone in this thread, over what I will argue is obsolete technology by the time it comes to market. It's not really that big of a deal. Name 3 features you think make this board better than anything else on the market and I guarantee you I can show you they are not the first to do any of them. There's nothing special or new about this board, it just looks like a solid board.

fuck you Evolve!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!
[/quote]

I rest my case.
```

```
[quote="evoheyax, post:430, topic:2510"]
My whole point is, you've been a fan boy from the beginning, eating up every little detail, and getting so hyped, and trying to hype up everyone in this thread, over what I will argue is obsolete technology by the time it comes to market. There's nothing special or new about this board, it just looks like a solid board.
[/quote]

What other non-DIY board is coming to market that is going to wipe the floor with the GT specs (if they are legit) by the time it hits the market? It is not about "features" for me. Simply put, the range they are advertising is highly appealing coming from 3.5-4.5 miles on a charge. I wouldn't care if I only got 10-15 miles (though I highly doubt it'd be that low). It'd still be better than what I had. This board isn't doing anything new in the esk8 world as a whole, but it is something that (if legit) will be far better than anything *commerically* available right now, and in the near future (unless another esk8 comes out of the blue). DIY builds by nature will always be ahead of the off-the-shelf boards -- just like PC games vs console. However if the board is real it will be all I need.

I rest my case.
```

## \#443 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-17T23:23:42.228Z Reads: 165

```
ahhh... I think we would all love an all weather water proof hub motor. But as far as I know, that hasn't been done. The issue is heat. You would want to seal up the hub from water, but you need vents for air flow or it will overheat super quick, especially being a hub motor. Technically, they are almost all water resistant. Motors generally don't care much about water. I've ridden my enertion r-spec motor in light rain many times, it eats it up and spits it right back out. Now there could be a build up of rust over time, and most importantly, the bearings will break due to rust first and formost. You would need a hub motor with ceramic bearings to solve that problem, then you would likely not have any issues. But you would also have to seal off any pcbs, like the speed controller and the receiver. The issue with that, is the speed controller needs some amount of air flow. Or it will over heat quickly. So there's a lot of problems to be solved with water proofing electric skateboards.
```

---

```
The reality is, the technology is there to make a water resistant board. Motors generally don't care about water in the short run. But you won't get year after year of use if you drown your motor in water frequently.
```

## \#451 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-18T02:11:19.580Z Reads: 174

```
I used to use enertion's belts. Now its hubs all the way, less maintenance, cleaner look, and easier to setup. 

about onloop, he left his own forum because he made a bunch of claims about how much better his stuff is then everyone else (its good stuff, there's no denying it), and everyone kept giving him shit and fighting with him (including me). If your going to make those kinds of claims, you need hard science to back you up, an he doesn't have it.

Sensored motors are great motors at low speed, but does nothing for mid to high speed. For this reason, most don't care about them. You can get the same results with a good kick push, and is also better for a belt and pulley system to do that.

With the VESC in FOC, you can get similar results without a sensor.

The big thing this GT board lacks in my opinion is stealth. Big motors, belt and pulley, and no FOC. When you look at the math, FOC is far better than BLDC, which all main brands are using.
```

## \#457 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-18T04:22:01.791Z Reads: 173

```
Honestly, you can put other wheels on them, you'd have to pour them from a mix, but the process is as simple as making jello. Or get rims cnc milled for you (Might not be a cheap option, but it's possible). You imagination is your limit.

Hubs are the lazy man (or beginner diy) option in my opinion. No need to assemble anything mechanically, which leaves just the electrical system. I've been thinking of selling kits for exactly this. It's like, the electric legos of e-boarding. I know the hurdles that are there. Tools are one, skills are another. Soldering is hard when you know little about it. It took me years to learn to solder well. Removing hurdles for beginners.
```

## \#535 Posted by: Michaelinvegas Posted at: 2016-05-20T19:10:58.420Z Reads: 169

```
The product that boosted wants to bring to the market is a super tidy product that their customers don't need to fiddle with....the non DIY types.... They target the iPhone user per se ..... Plug in to charge ...when you wanna use it... Grab and go....

I think bb and evolves target markets are slightly different...and it shows in looks, functionality, performance and thier commercials...so different, highlighting different uses (BB comes from a fun, practical, small EV, last mile stand point...Evolve comes from a premium Fun, the Porsche of electric boards, you can ride anything stand point) 

Also Boosted is a Kickstarter starlet ... And Evolve was built in a more traditional sense....

Two different boards. Two different companies. Two different target markets. (Of course at a point they overlap)

I would say they biggest competion that these two companies face in the future is not each other or another company per se but actually the DIY community. The easier it is to build at home...will give the consumer a reason to pause before they click that " buy " button
```

```
It will hit 26mph on 97s with the standard drive wheel. The 38 tooth drive wheel will increase torque but reduce top speed.
```

## \#814 Posted by: Jinra Posted at: 2016-05-25T22:28:30.271Z Reads: 149

```
It'd go 30.88mph with 90mm wheels and 33.28 with 97mm wheels. This is 100% efficient, however. It'll most likely go 70%~ of that. The 27mph rating of the raptor with 83mm wheels is also at 100% efficiency, so I doubt the Raptor would go as fast as advertised.

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/a/abfcf7bd753c3a0999307ec4379f22406a43829b.png" width="384" height="500">

If you take a look at the raptor mono video (who's motor has the same kV rating as the dual). he's traveling on a race track which is 440 yards or 400 meters. He made it 1 lap in 39 seconds. Doing the math he's traveling at 23mph.

EDIT: However, if you tweak the numbers and use 11.3 as the number of cells to simulate a 10s setup at full charge (42v). You can get 32.18mph at 100% efficiency and 25.74 at 80% efficiency. The reason I use 80% is because the mono got 23mph in a real world test vs the theoretical limit of 28.48 which equates to 80%.
```

---


## \#820 Posted by: Jinra Posted at: 2016-05-25T22:44:15.529Z Reads: 144

```
I'm just presenting the scientific data. All this is assuming everything is within spec. It could be the 6355 motor runs at higher than 190kV or some other factors. It's just with the assumption that the motor turns 190rpm per volt of power, it can only reach the speeds I've shown unless it was going downhill.

Like I said at 80% efficiency it can reach 25.74 mph at 100% battery. It may be more efficient if you have a tail wind, or are a lighter rider.
```

## \#822 Posted by: Jinra Posted at: 2016-05-25T22:49:27.535Z Reads: 141

```
Here's some good news. My calculations are actually slightly off since the 440 yard distance was assuming he was on the inner most lane of the track. Since Jason said he rode in the middle of the track, it makes the distance he was traveling a bit further. You may get a slight bit more speed than what I said, but keep in mind that numbers are numbers and these are the actual limits of the hardware. Try playing around with the calculator if you're curious.

http://toddy616.blogspot.com/2013/07/electric-skateboard-calculator.html?m=1
```

## \#849 Posted by: magnetvox Posted at: 2016-05-26T04:20:53.374Z Reads: 140

```
I find it amusing following the 'which board is better' discussions. I like the car analogies and I'll offer my own. I've had rotaries, fast fours, turbos sixes, and v8s. People side passionately with one over the other, the reality is they all have different strengths and weaknesses and to be honest, I enjoyed them all depending on what I needed at the time. Torque vs power vs efficiency vs handling vs style. Embrace the diversity, it is what gives us choice and caters to all our wants/ needs. Rather than getting fixated on speed, range, torque, aesthetics, the discussion should be about the design philosophies behind each builder. That goes for DIY too. Those philosophies give insight into the strengths of each board. Jason is openly an industry disruptor and enthusiast with a passion for raw torque/ speed numbers and short/ agile development cycles.  Evolved guys seem like chilled surfers with long development cycles and an eye for aesthetics. The Boosted crew invest energy into smart electronics, 'cool kid' factors, and a prioritization of  air portability over range (their blog shows how they diverge in terms of design priorities/ decisions, as does Jason's Vlogs). Matching your needs/wants/ resources with the appropriate design is the name of the game. Not endless pissing contests and a focus on "Which is fastest today, show me the video". If we didn't have so many different approaches, this shit would be boring as all hell and we wouldn't have any choice. Sorry for the rant, but I feel this forum is smarter than this sudden fixation on GT looks vs Raptor speed vs Boosted V2 range vs DIY cost rubbish. Have the discussion, but keep it balanced and enjoy the differences.  The industry is in a really healthy place, and as with all tech based industries, there will be a constant leap frogging of industry leaders (however you define that) depending on their new design release dates, or what you think is more important for you.
```

---
## \#850 Posted by: Dedbny Posted at: 2016-05-26T04:22:10.478Z Reads: 135

```
Enertion have claimed more range with higher top speed avg. 40-45km/hr. But my limited testing  is othrwise. If your going more conservatively shouldnt you get more range. Unless you are running around a ring like in his video and at a consistant speed and all hunched down its proobably possible. Ive been riding it on random path, grades and speeds.

Battery life will deteriorate with top speed. Its simple as that. But then go down hill and pick up regenerative braking. Thatbis the trick. You shouls always have a little more juice left even on the limit to get home if you use that braking advantage.

One again unless yourve seen it in real life dont make such a bold statement. Ive seen the GT in real life as well, its a great looking board in comparison. They are all different.

Its all about the GT love here. Cant wait to try the production version.

@magnetvox agree. The theads always get highjacked. Let the reall testing Begin. Im just giving my side with commentaary. We all love or hate for whatever reason its all a mattee of your own taste.
```

## \#855 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-26T05:11:43.278Z Reads: 129

```
@magnetvox I've said to people many times that there isn't a "best board" because no board can do everything... The GT is king of range right now in the complete market, the Raptor in top speed and torque, the BB in comfort/reliability, and Inboard/Stary for hub motors. They all offer unique things and we should all get the boards that work for our needs/lifestyle.

Personally, I'm a speed demon. But I also love exploring, and going places I would never want to walk (for long). So I got the Raptor and the GT to play with. Now I will never have to compromise! :) 

Unfortunately for my pockets I will likely be getting the 90mm wheels and 97mm wheels to swap between the GT and the carbon...probably closer to fall though because my wallet is literally dying screaming at me to stop!
```

## \#868 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-26T12:06:42.900Z Reads: 133

```
You cannot compare the prices across different currencies for a distributor that is not **yours**. It does not make sense.........the only way you would be getting it cheaper in Australia than US people were getting it here is if you use **USD** in **Australia** shipping **to** Australia. They will not take pre-orders that are not local. Even though it seems like you can pre-order from them because the prices change for the board it is not so, I believe you can purchase other things and have it shipped to you and that is why they have that converter...
```

## \#872 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-05-26T13:13:32.065Z Reads: 136

```
[quote="Kelvinski, post:864, topic:2510, full:true"]
Interesting towards the end of the video where it states 0-25mph (40kph) in 3 seconds compared to what I read previously, where someone said 5-6 seconds? Also, I thought the 83mm used in the video could only reach 22mph (36kph)
[/quote]


I don't know where they got those numbers from...doesn't look like they legit tested it with any tools. I got my 5-6 second estimate from the beta testers I've talked to have actually tested it. As far as top speed Evolve themselves have made a chart for what it should be. The video didn't say anything about which wheels got that speed because they likely themselves don't even know. I will be testing when I get mine and show via phone app and remote speedometer what the top speed is with AT and stock street wheels.

@BrabRS a lot of the beta testers / ambassadors are probably over hyping it. What many people don't realize is that a lot of these testers are coming from a **single** drive (evolve) eboard. So when they call the GT "beastly" or talk about how "dangerous" it is I think it is because they have never ridden something with two motors lol. At worst I expect that it will be a bit punchier than the d+ with the standard gears and a lot more punchier with the 38T gear. Hopefully I'm wrong and it flat out is noticeably better than the d+, but I have rarely, if ever, seen someone compare the torque to the d+ (fairly without bias). After riding the d+ for ~700 miles I have a nice reference point to see how "beastly" the torque is. Seems like there are a lot of new boarders that have been demo-ing these boards as well which explains some of these reviews. 

As far as range though it meets its claims, I don't doubt that the range tests that have been done are legit.
```

## \#941 Posted by: Ermac-514 Posted at: 2016-05-30T01:43:21.815Z Reads: 147

```
Kevlar vs Carbon fiber
What it comes down to are what we engineers call "Material Properties" specifically ultimate strength, stiffness, and facture toughness.

Carbon fibre has a high ultimate strength (the force required to break it) and a very high stiffness (the amount it stretches/bends when force is applied to it). Fiberglass, Kevlar, and carbon fiber have all got approximatley the same strength and are stronger than aluminum or steel. Carbon fiber is far stiffer than aluminum, steel, fiberglass, and Kevlar. This makes carbon fiber ideal for making a strong, light, stiff structure and is why we use it.

The downside of carbon fibre is that it is brittle (has low fracture toughness). You can easily cut thin sheets or cloth with scissors. Carbon fibre cracks easilly particularly in cases where the force is quickly applied (during impact loading such as a crash, it can shatter). Furthermore, once it cracks a bit, the crack can easily grow longer and a cracked structure (wings, fuselage) is not a good thing.

Kevlar on the other hand, has a particularly high fracture toughness. It is much harder to crack, very difficult to cut cleanly even with very sharp scissors, and stands up well to impact loads. That's why it is used for bullet-proof vests.

So, when choosing a composite material to use as a reinforcement, you look at what type of loads the area being reinforced will like see. Kevlar is a great choice as a reinforcement in the upper wingskin over the main retrct in a Bandit for example. If you land hard enough to break the flex plates, the Kevlar has a better chance of stopping the aluminum frame of the retract unit from cutting through the upper wingskin. Caron fibre, with its high strength and stiffness is a good choice for a wing spar since you want a strong and stiff wing. You can also use it in the fuselage or structure to add strength or stiffness but it would not be a good choice in corners of cutouts since it can crack.<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/d/dad961a18745c85ee735913c47f71ed14a4443c2.jpeg" width="690" height="459">
```

---

```
ou do not drain them under 10% and do not charge them over 80% but I have heard somewhere in this forum that you want to charge your batteries once in a while to full charge because all the balancing of the bms happens at the end of the charge cycle so that your batteries stay in balance charge them once in a while to 100%

You're biggest enemy is over discharging...you can't over charge...bms is suppose to do that...the balancing ... That happens the moment you plug it in...as you get closer to full charge the amps going in the battery slow to trickle ...then stops
```

## \#1022 Posted by: magnetvox Posted at: 2016-06-01T06:13:45.893Z Reads: 163

```
All batteries have strengths and weaknesses. In my experience, any rechargeable lithium battery can vent to atmosphere if the conditions are right, and the possibility of fire with any high voltage/ current electronics device application is a no brainer. How high that possibility is- well we probably need statistics and studies, not forum posts as references (not saying it didnâ€™t happen- statistically speaking I believe it probably has).

Back to strengths and weaknesses- if you select a cheaper battery with a shorter shelf or cycle life, economically is it better or worse? Depends on cost/ range analysis. If you fit a larger battery system in a smaller form factor, and it goes further than an alternative on each charge, but has less cycles available- again it may or may not be better. Eg, You can go 12 km 2000 times, or you can go 30 km 800 times, at the same cost, then its arguably the same outcome. How you actually use the board though, and your charging habits, with alter the perception of economy one way or the other. 

In my experience (not with skateboards but with military radio systems) the environment makes a massive difference in any battery performance. Some chemistries are more resistant than others, but they are all affected. Very cold weather absolutely kills performance. Extremely hot weather and direct sunlight drastically increases the chances of venting and/or fire.  I think the different perceptions people have will be heavily guided by the location you are in. I never see snow, and so my experience with battery life and range will be vastly different to someone who does, when comparing the exact same chemistry. 

People who are new to e-boards scour these forums long after they have been written. Posting assumptions dressed up as facts about batteries in general undermines the process of learning from each other. Also, arguing on one consideration alone about why one battery solution is better than the other is a bit asinine. Argue based on a complete assessment of life vs cost vs form factor vs cycles vs charging costs vs environmental performance preferences vs portability (air vs land only), versus safety record, and if possible clarify facts vs assumptions. Otherwise this is a bit of a wasted discussion because we go around in circles.
```

---
## \#1023 Posted by: Ermac-514 Posted at: 2016-06-01T15:21:02.671Z Reads: 163

```
[quote="magnetvox, post:1022, topic:2510"]
the environment makes a massive difference in any battery performance. Some chemistries are more resistant than others, but they are all affected. Very cold weather absolutely kills performance. Extremely hot weather and direct sunlight drastically increases the chances of venting and/or fire.  I think the different perceptions people have will be heavily guided by the location you are in
[/quote]

I agree 100%
```

## \#1028 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-06-01T19:55:15.724Z Reads: 160

```
Actually, I want to talk more :slight_smile:

It's seems no different internally from the raptor. Same logic, also a 10s lion battery. Still can't find the number of p, by the size, it looks like 3p or 4p, which would make it the same config as the space cell. I don't see how that battery pack gives 31 miles... I would like more info about their setup, but have yet to see anymore details about the battery (Ah, Wh, ...), so I still don't believe that number is even remotely accurate. Its about as thin as you can get a board with lion batteries, so bravo to them for that, but I don't like bs numbers that suck people into to buy, only to find the range is very different later. If they would give more details (like enertion does), it would be easy to tell if that is the case here or not.

If you look at their spec sheet of wheels, they give the different top speeds for each size of wheel. But, when you go to buy, they say up to 26 mph. There's no disclosure that the size of the wheel matters. It's shady IMO to put information the way they do. They say there's a few factors that MAY impact distance and top speed numbers. But as a consumer, if I didn't know better, I would believe that i might at worst get 27 miles of range and 24 mph top speed. The top speed for the 83mm wheels are not even that high, so people are going to order and not realize they aren't really getting what they want because of the way the information is presented in a misleading way IMO.

- my two cents
```

## \#1043 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-06-01T21:22:35.572Z Reads: 152

```
[quote="evoheyax, post:1028, topic:2510"]
If you look at their spec sheet of wheels, they give the different top speeds for each size of wheel. But, when you go to buy, they say up to 26 mph. There's no disclosure that the size of the wheel matters.
[/quote]
Don't know which distributors site you're on but....
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/a/a64d2e24dbfafd4974a8888b77ef8106dbb0d572.png" width="427" height="500">

I will admit that the US site does not have the speed chart like the AUS site does. There's a lot of hiccups between different distrib sites. But this disclaimer does exist on all of the distrib sites if they are carrying the GT and copy pasted the specs. 

[quote="evoheyax, post:1028, topic:2510"]
It's shady IMO to put information the way they do.
[/quote]

It's not much worse than Boosted honestly. Boosted has been claiming the D+ goes 22mph when in fact it only hits that speed for a millisecond in pro and then maintains speed at 20mph. Boosted has also claimed their board gets 6 or 7 miles when in fact users rarely see that range unless they are on all flats or in eco. 

[quote="evoheyax, post:1028, topic:2510"]
I don't like bs numbers that suck people into to buy, only to find the range is very different later.
[/quote]

The range will always depend on your environment and especially your riding style. Companies probably don't bother doing extensive testing to come up with charts because it is practically impossible to capture all the factors enough to form a real-life range expectancy. There could be more disclosure of this fact, but then people wouldn't even have a rough number to really go off of when they consider how much range they have. The truth is that it is a relative number and no one can precisely predict your range except you. 

[quote="evoheyax, post:1028, topic:2510"]
But as a consumer, if I didn't know better, I would believe that i might at worst get 27 miles of range and 24 mph top speed.
[/quote]
Again, as a consumer, if you were really concerned about this you would wait either find someone with the board and ask them to test or wait for it to be reviewed. The people who get excited at the specs and jump at it should already know the risk in getting something they have not seen tested. This is not Evolve's first long range board, which is one of the reasons why I don't believe they are BS'ing about this one, and I don't think the tests out there are fake -- despite your doubts. 

[quote="evoheyax, post:1028, topic:2510"]
The top speed for the 83mm wheels are not even that high, so people are going to order and not realize they aren't really getting what they want because of the way the information is presented in a misleading way IMO.
[/quote]

On the US website and possibly others I believe this is the case because their speed chart is missing. But technically for everyone else it is their own fault for not looking closely at the specifications. I'm not surprised they would market the board like this the same way Boosted does marketing 22mph -- except Boosted doesn't really go 22mph (for long).

[quote="evoheyax, post:1033, topic:2510"]
I don't see anything indicating what range you could expect in different riding environments (like a data sheet).
[/quote]
This would have to be a pretty robust data sheet that has to take in a shit ton of variables: wind, height, weight, temperature, hill grade, acceleration/breaking habits, speed change habits, etc. Too much to track. This could be done by a third party. But it would still just be a bunch of numbers thrown around since conditions in the real world change to such an extent that they can skew testing results imo.
```

## \#1044 Posted by: OwenGrady Posted at: 2016-06-01T21:28:35.951Z Reads: 133

```
The absolute funniest part of your statement is that you state Evolve offers no facts to back up their claims, yet this thread is littered with posts of the information they have made public, proven from their testing.

They offer flat ground ideal testing, because this is the only way to come near a consistent repeatable number. If your area has two hills, and my area has one, then i will get better results than you on any board. Very simple. This is not Evolve being sketchy, its Evolve showing exactly how they achieved this number, and how you could too.

Hills, weight, setup, riding style, how many pink mojitos you drink, are all variables that affect this number. To cater for every possibility is ludicrously difficult and to be honest - not enough return on the time invested to do.

The GT customers will prove the numbers. You can either be part of it, or be left to turn back early when your battery is flat.

If you want the numbers for your style of riding, test it yourself.

So far Evolve is the only one who has come to the table and been very public about its performance. They also offer it in a $2k product that works straight out of the box. No assembly required.
```

## \#1046 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-06-01T21:45:57.425Z Reads: 129

```
It's not that you have to cater to every possibility, but there's two really main factors that will affect top speed and range, and those are rider weight and hills. Wind can't be tested for, it's unpredictable and changes dirrections too frequently in the real world, and in most places, is not an issue. My point is they don't even post a margin of error, because they don't bother testing to know. Eliminating these large variables would reduce the margin of error in their numbers, and give more transparency.

There's too much conversation in here to see every bit of information in this thread. This threads purpose was speculation and discussion, not to be informative about the board. And while yes, their are bits of information found here not on evolves website, It's near impossible to find it all due to the number of posts.

I have yet to see any video showing range testing. You can engineer a range test to be really good (i.e ride down hills and flat only, never up hills, calculate the exact most efficient speed and ride at that, ect.), that has been my whole point all along. And I've yet to see a good any company produce good information that can be used for comparing the pre-made boards out there.

They have many different configurations of gears and wheels. They show one going up a steep hill (barely) and another doing acceleration, and another speed. And All three videos I saw of those where a different configuration. It's hard to get torque and top speed. gearing and wheel size will affect both of these numbers. So it's possible to make this a torque machine, it's possible to go a fair speed, nothing doing both in the same config, and even then, that's one config. Not all configs will climb steep hills, not all configs will get the same speed. Picking different configs that highlight good torque and decent top speeds are separately is cool, but misleading IMO.

This is a science and math heavy field, yet, I see little science or math being presented...
```

## \#1111 Posted by: Ermac-514 Posted at: 2016-06-09T13:44:31.111Z Reads: 139

```
This is for e  bike  But is Worth it to read

There are a lot of factors that affect the range of the electric bike, such as:

What power assist setting you are using?  Most power assist bikes have 4 assist levels.  Some e-bikes just have a throttle that you can vary the assist with.  This is pretty common sense, but the more assist you use the less range you will have.

Are you climbing a lot of hills?  Range goes down.

Are you riding into a lot of headwinds? Range goes down.

Are you carrying heavy cargo on your bike? Range does down.

Some bikes may have a very inefficient motor (lost energy in the motor due to friction, etc.) that causes decreased range, but these days most electric bike motors are fairly efficient (there is room for improvement!)

What is the condition of your bike?  A well adjusted bike goes farther i.e. well lubricated chain, proper tire pressure, etc.

What is your tire pressure?  Lower pressures = less range.   There is a nice balance between too high a pressure (not comfortable) and too low a pressure (not efficient).  50-60 psi is a good pressure range for street riding.

Are you pedaling at the right times?  Pedaling at critical moments (when accelerating or climbing), you will go farther.

Pedal more => More range and better health ðŸ™‚

If you are concerned with range I recommend going with a large capacity battery pack.  Some electric bike manufacturers have use a standard 10 ah pack with an option to upgrade to say a 15 ah pack.
```

## \#1118 Posted by: magnetvox Posted at: 2016-06-10T03:37:04.117Z Reads: 124

## \#1119 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-06-10T03:56:37.838Z Reads: 139

```
Haven't gotten toooooooo in depth with the plans but I have ideas as to what I want to do. I've been focusing on getting the things I know I need to have to up my current production value (I've been making youtube videos for a while). One of the big purchases being a nice fluid tripod head and a slider for some more cinematic shots when I'm doing voice overs instead of just my face : p. Some interesting go pro mounts for shots while riding, and a more portable mic I can take with me while on the go and possibly record while riding. Really pumped to test it all out.

As for tests off the top of my head:

* An accurate hill climbing test **with no cuts**, making sure to show the board(s) fully charged, the hill gradient, and a split screen to show that I am applying full throttle. Also stats on my weight, show current winds, temperature, and my clothing. 

* Top speed test with the 83mm, 97mm (knock off flywheels), and stock AT wheels. On flats, going up long hills, etc. 

* Braking test, same idea with all wheels above, maybe use some chalk and bring a ruler to measure distance. Also test on different inclines as well. 

* RANGE TEST, this will probably be the hardest to do and take multiple videos. still thinking about how best to do this. The first one will be in GT mode on the street set up with the 83mm, likely on a flat terrain in the city, going around a pre-designated area a bunch during a time of day where cars are less likely to be around. Won't be all that realistic but for those that do bike paths it might be. Following that will be a number of tests in different scenarios such as: commuting to work in the city, commuting in a hilly suburby area, cruising on bike paths, etc. I will pretty much entirely leave out AT for these tests because almost no one has really given a good go at street testing besides one guy that only did it in ECO mode. Still thinking of more ideas but this will be a lot...

* Sososoo many more things to make videos about, but I will try to condense them a bit depending on the subject matter, the above deserve videos standalone and are what I see most people concerned about so I will try to make good videos on them. It will be a very busy summer for me :D 

Currently just learning how to use my tools better and also collect as much information ahead of time as I can.
```

## \#1189 Posted by: LordofTaco Posted at: 2016-06-14T07:17:48.036Z Reads: 126

```
Hey guys, I'm new here but thought you guys might have some questions?
My board just arrived today and I took it out for a spin once before it got dark, this thing is a beast!

A few little notes so far:
The battery indicator is great however it varies a LOT, one moment I'm going up a hill and it's on 4% and then the next I'm speeding along a flat and its showing 46%.
The breaks are very responsive (almost too much, I fell off once already just from breaking too hard)
The carbon fibre makes it look amazing but it scuffs up very easily, already got a decent amount on the bottom unfortunatley (from breaking too hard and scraping it, but that's my bad riding)
If you guys have any questions, or want any tests done let me know
```

## \#1198 Posted by: LordofTaco Posted at: 2016-06-14T09:36:44.631Z Reads: 134

```
I was very very impressed with the range, I'm keen to do a full range test of normal 'fun' riding, and then trying to get the best range possible to see what it is. @Rob.Endless christ man, I really hope you never fall that CF helmet is overkill if you're new...you will have to bail at some point especially with the GT lol everyone has at least one fall. As far as bearings save yourself some money and just use Zealous. Especially if you plan on switching wheels often. Built in spacers and speed rings will save you a lot of time.
```

```
Kegel and 

Abec/evolve etc....( this should fit most other compatible wheels..
Excluding 38 tooth...
Pretty sure.
```

## \#1320 Posted by: Jinra Posted at: 2016-06-16T18:48:38.116Z Reads: 151

```
I don't think the 38T is meant for the 107mm flywheel as it seems the issue with the 107's is that they're too wide for the current pulley. 38T is meant for 83-97 fly wheels for more torque and lower top speed.
```

## \#1337 Posted by: Jinra Posted at: 2016-06-17T04:30:19.885Z Reads: 160

```
If anyone is interested, I did some calculations based on various videos and info and found the street setup has a 2.133... ratio with 15T/32T. It does 37km/h with 80mm wheels which leads to the motor having a 130kv rating. This is in comparison to @chaka's similar motors at 170/200kv
```

## \#1338 Posted by: magnetvox Posted at: 2016-06-17T05:18:16.871Z Reads: 175

```
Ok, so the rain clear and I just had my first hit out. I'll do a quick review of my thoughts. For context- I've not ridden any other electric skateboard so I don't have any benchmarks. But I'm also not someone who trumpets something just to avoid buyers remorse or to enter a pissing contest on who's board is better. For the cool kids (DIYers)- I haven't built my own board yet, so I'm a filthy complete owner for now, don't fear, a build project is starting to form and will be underway soon. 

So, the GT. First thing that struck me was the engineering. This is a well put together piece of kit. First ride was 1-2 hours, nothing came loose, everything worked as advertised, no random noises etc. It just did what it was suppose to do straight up. 

I have undulating hills around me, mixed in with smooth flat areas, and the odd step hill. You need to be in fast or GT mode to eat hills. The board easily rode every hill that you would want to ride a board up and down for fun. According to the controller, I did 21 km on my first ride, and had 71% charge when I got back. The regenerative braking contributed to that I suspect, given every-time I went up, I could find a good long coast back down. Plus I wasn't breaking any land-speed records on my first run. 

The next thing that hit me were the brakes. Rock solid. Like your first car, you get fixated first on speed, then on acceleration, and then you realise brakes are probably more important for going fast. Because they get you out of trouble and give you confidence to push things. 

The remote is excellent. I found the trigger mechanism is sensitive but I dialled into it after about 5-10 mins. The benefit to the sensitivity is the fidelity on the control. You can accelerate and brake as finely as you like, as long as you don't get carried away in the moment. I wore snap-on mechanics gloves- they are designed to give you dexterity in your fingers and they worked really well with the fine trigger control. The control sits comfortably in your hand, and it was handy being able to check speed, distance and battery in front of you by bringing up your hand momentarily.  

I spent about 2 mins in slow, 10 mins in eco, the rest in fast. Once it completely is dry outside, and I feel I'm qualified to not kill myself, I'll give the GT mode a go. I found I rode mostly between 20-30 km/h after maybe the first 10-20mins of WTF am I doing. I've never ridden one before and it was that straightforward to get up and moving. 

Carving. You can tell this thing was built with carving in mind. It was very stable at straight line speed but if you get into carving that is where it really shines. Buttery smooth is how I would describe it, and I've only been carving since morning tea so that is saying something. I thought I'd be more of a point-to-point kind of person but the carving was the most enjoyable aspect of the ride. 

The board layout works. My feet felt locked in on the W concave and the slight drop down. I got better at tight turns as I went. I suspect a regular rider would turn this thing on a dime. I'm use to kicktails and had to adjust to leaning heavily into tight turns at low speed, like when I wanted to turn around on a hill. You do have to pick it up in tight situations, and the board is heavy, and big, no doubt. There is nothing really to pick it up with, which makes it a subtle challenge to lift, but the smooth, flat carbon belly makes it easy to carry like you would a normal board, once you have it in hand. 

21kms down, and I didn't come off once; that has more to do with the fact this thing is just well designed and very balanced. I watched the videos on this forum on how to ride the Raptor and that shit works. Lean forward, accelerate, lean back, brake. The fine grain control meant I didn't get launched, but I had to think about it or it will launch you. Loads of torque but it is dialled in to be accessible. 

The ride was very comfortable. The stock road wheels are excellent, but again I have no reference point. They just feel smooth, forgiving, and just grippy enough. I hit a cats eye going uphill at about 20km/h early on and the board didn't flinch. Less speed might be an issue, but I didn't get caught on any debris or cracks.   

No controller dropouts or anything. Which I realised is important if you want to enjoy hooking in a bit harder. 

People stop and stare. One bloke lost his mind when I was crossing near a pedestrian crossing. They are a good looking board up close. Others just cant work out what you are doing, especially if you are moving like a boss.  

Cars are pretty dangerous. For whatever reason they seem less comfortable passing that if you are on a bike. Doesn't help that the quest for smooth road tends to pull you out from the edge maybe a bit more than normal. I just found I couldn't predict what drivers would do as well as I can on a bike, maybe you are harder to see or they don't expect you to move so fast on a board, or both. Didn't have any real issues but I was cautious near cars after seeing some random moves. You cover ground fast so need to think ahead about other road users. Momentum governs your braking distance more than the brakes, as you can brake harder than your posture can support. 

There was still patchy water on the road- no issues. I realised early I I needed to look ahead a bit further than on a normal board because potholes and puddles come up quick. I didn't push my luck, if I went through some surface water on the road, I kept it slow until the wheels dried (5-10 secs) and then got back into it. 

Fun factor- excellent. I use to jump out of planes for a living and it's been a while since I've had that really fun kick. No different to skiing or snow boarding in that sense, but strange because you can do it on the streets behind your house. I really enjoyed it. 

The board came in AT mode. Changing over to road took about 10 mins (first time so some of that was double checking) but it was simple enough. I haven't tried the AT wheels/ mode yet. 

In summary- impressed. Even at the price I felt no remorse (which I was expecting). I rode probably as long as my novice legs would carry me in a first hit out, and I had enough charge to do it 3 times over. This board is a legit transport replacement in good weather if you wanted it to be. It's not last mile, its the whole journey. Pretty good bit of engineering, they did their homework and executed it well. 

Will see how it holds up with more testing etc.

Edit- spelling and grammar
```

---

## \#1348 Posted by: magnetvox Posted at: 2016-06-17T21:45:33.283Z Reads: 158

```
Yeah, good question- depends on interpretation. It has excellent brakes and will bring you to a complete stop on inclines but once you are stationary it is only momentary. It won't hold the board there. So if you are going up hill and you brake to a complete halt, I found it would then lightly start roll back unless I applied a small amount of throttle to hold it in place. Does that make sense?

How do other boards do it? 

I imagine it is so the board doesn't draw current once you are stopped? Or perhaps a limitation of the esc logic? Or because it separates braking from reverse?

I definitely noticed it though because intuitively (without having ridden an e-board before) I assumed the board would hold in place if I kept the brake on while stationary on an incline, but it didn't. 

I'll confirm today for sure, but that is what I recall.
```

## \#1351 Posted by: Mr_Mahal Posted at: 2016-06-17T22:10:59.211Z Reads: 151

```
Well, the Boosted board uses "Fred Flintstone" style breaks which means it basically throws itself into reverse to get you to a complete stop. Technically the BB doesn't come to a complete stop in a sense without you applying throttle in the appropriate direction which is what @magnetvox describes he has to do to keep the board in place.

So if you wanted to come to a complete stop AND hold it in place going **downhill** then you'd want to apply the breaks in acceleration mode, and once coming to a stop put in reverse and lightly apply the throttle....I guess really the point is going by what @magnetvox you DO come to a complete stop which the entire purpose of the breaks, to hold it there you can just step off or do as I described but I don't understand why that's necessary unless you just want to look cool lol
```

---

## \#1353 Posted by: LordofTaco Posted at: 2016-06-17T22:51:23.110Z Reads: 150

```
The breaks do keep you rolling very slowly on hills, you come to a complete stop and then you'll roll very slowly, but it's not an issue as you can just step off the board at this point? Unless you wanna look 'cool' like Mr_ mahal said, but I feel like you'd look 'cooler' if you have the control to slow down, and then just step off casually when you've come to a stop as if nothing happened.
The board does roll relatively well when you're not using it as an electric board so maybe this has something to do with it? A normal long board will roll down a hill, and so does this one.
```
